    <li> I really researched makeup brush sets on Amazon and other makeup review sites. I have never had a set of brushes so I wanted to read lots of feedback and see ratings so I would choose wisely. I, also, didn&#x27;t want to be overwhelmed with too many very specific purpose brushes as a newbie. I read the reviews on this set and the rating was very high.     <li> Niece was overjoyed at receiving these for Christmas. I picked them up because they had much better reviews for durability than similar brush sets.</li>
    <li> Soft brushes! Love these</li>
    <li> I rarely write reviews, but I wanted to write one about this one because it&#x27;s an awesome deal if you know how to properly care for inexpensive makeup brushes.  I am somewhat of a beauty product aficionado and I have a lot of makeup brushes, both high end and inexpensive.  These are really great! They are dense and shaped really well.  I like the kabuki style brushes for foundation and cream products, which these are amazing for! The synthetic bristles make them very easy to clean as well.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;The downside with these brushes is that they aren&#x27;t super well put-together. That is easily fixable though. You just need a hot glue gun and a pen (or pen-like object). Here&#x27;s what I do:&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;1) Wash them thoroughly.  They do have that factory chemical smell that comes from all inexpensive brushes ordered from China. Let them dry.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) Separate the handle from the brush head.  Yes, I separated the handle. These are not glued in well, so people who complain of the brushes breaking or the bristles coming out, this is why. Because there is not much glue holding them together, the handles will detach fairly easily.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) Put hot glue in the back side of the brush head.  BE CAREFUL, THE METAL PART WILL GET HOT (I ADVISE USING GLOVES FOR THIS PART).  Pour some hot glue in the back of the brush head and GENTLY pat it down with the pen.  This will help secure the bristles a little better.  Then put some hot glue around the rim of the brush head and quickly insert the handle.  This will help secure the handle on more effectively.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did this with all of my brushes (and I have used this technique on other inexpensive brands as well) and it works well. Yes, it requires a little extra work to make these last long term, however for the price, I think it&#x27;s worth it.  The only other complaint I might have is that these soak up a lot moisture, so when you dry them after washing, try to dry them upside down.  Otherwise, a great buy!</li>
